<span id="freeTextContainer12121968680246792740"><b>5 'Holy Fucking Christ, Dear Sweet Mother of God' this book was fucking AWESOME stars</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413283i/813508._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>Being gay wasn’t like changing eye colors; you couldn’t just get contacts and “Whammo!”— gayness.</i>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413283i/813509._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>"I like you. Even though you’re probably a criminal and are going to get me thrown off the force. And you kicked me. Broke my nose. Made me gay and refused to kiss me."</i>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have to warn you in advance, when I get excited about something, I tend to swear like a sailor with tourette's syndrome. You've been warned.</span>
  <span id="freeText12121968680246792740" style="display:none"><b>5 'Holy Fucking Christ, Dear Sweet Mother of God' this book was fucking AWESOME stars</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413283i/813508._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>Being gay wasn’t like changing eye colors; you couldn’t just get contacts and “Whammo!”— gayness.</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413283i/813509._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>"I like you. Even though you’re probably a criminal and are going to get me thrown off the force. And you kicked me. Broke my nose. Made me gay and refused to kiss me."</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have to warn you in advance, when I get excited about something, I tend to swear like a sailor with tourette's syndrome. You've been warned...<b> FUCKITY FUCKING FUCK</b> but this book was awesome! I don't even have the words to describe how much I loved it. I'm pretty sure I highlighted every single word that came out of Austin's mouth. I couldn't stop myself. He was like a lingual Midas. Everything that came out of the man's mouth was pure gold.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413283ra/813510.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">I wasn’t gay. You don’t go twenty-six years before the gay gene suddenly just kicks in. It didn’t work like that. I was sure of it. Not that I knew that much about being gay. I had one friend with same-sex orientation, and Dana hadn’t spoken to me since I asked her to describe her honeymoon in graphic detail— and then made vibrator noises.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>Awww, Austin, don't fret<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413283ra/813511.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Fuck it, I’m not gay. Goddammit. I’m bunny-slipper-sexual?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>Really? Done and DONE!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413283i/813512._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Now come to mama Austin!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was like the perfect set up for a joke: A detective, a whore, and a demonic looking cat walk into a diner...<br><br>But I digress, so let's get to the review shall we?<br><br>Austin Glass seemingly has it all, a great job as a detective with the FBI lined up, a more than healthy trust fund that keeps him in $2000 suits for work, a charming personality that seems to get him whatever he wants, a wise crack for every occasion, and a loving fiance. There's just one problem that he seems to have now. After seeing a certain redheaded busboy in bunny slippers, Austin can't seem to stop thinking about him. Which proves to be a bit of a problem. How does a man that has been engaged 4 times, and cheated on each woman with the next one, all of a sudden find himself fantasizing about<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413283ra/813513.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">I’m not gay."<br>"Congratulations. Would you like a medal?" Bunny Slippers asked. <br>"I already have a medal. For bravery, not for being gay. I think you made me gay." <br>"I made you gay? Is that better or worse than the person who made you stupid?"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>That is quite the conundrum you got yourself there Austin. Perhaps there's a book you can read that might help you out?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413283ra/813514.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Hmmm....well maybe you can talk to a gay friend or something? Maybe talk to your partner's gay daughter? I think he offered...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">I don’t give a shit if your daughter is gay or your whole fucking lineage is taking it up the ass. They’re not me. Unless you have some unique perspective on why I’m suddenly checking out guys’ asses, then I’m just going to go with the redhead that takes it up the ass and hope he has a shitfucking answer." Or a goddamn roadmap of how to deal with a sudden attraction to penises might be helpful, too.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Well sure, I guess you could do that too.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I think I read this entire book with a big goofy grin on my face. I don't think there was one thing about it I disliked. Everything was just fucking awesome!<br><br><b>Austin's internal musings</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Dear God, he’d broken my nose, charged me for sex, kicked me, made me look like an idiot, and all I wanted to do is bang the sense out of him with my dick.<br></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Austin's banter with his partner</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Today is hump day, Luis." I lolled my head to the side and blinked prettily at my partner. <br>"Don’t make me lock you in a cell, Glass." <br>"What kind of gifts do people give their partner on hump day? Lube? Vibrators? Issues of Bazooms with a box of tissues?"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>And most especially, Austin's banter with Peter</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">You’re frustrating." <br>"I’m adorable." <br>"From a distance," Peter admitted— grudgingly.<br>"Up close, I’m sexy as hell." <br>"You’re rich, spoiled and used to getting your way," he said stubbornly. <br>"Not true. If I had my way you would have kissed me and ridden me like cowboy while screaming ‘yeehaw’."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This book had everything; humor, suspense, mystery, action. And when we finally have some action between Peter and Austin...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413283ra/813515.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Major swoon!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380389135i/750132._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>How the fuckidy fuck did I go so long without reading this book? What is wrong with me? Wait! Don't answer that. But in all seriousness, this book was simply the best. <b>Thank you my PPE, Pervy, for giving me the friendly shove to read this one. You are the bestest!</b> *muah*<br><br>Now I could probably keep sitting here and ramble on and on about how much I loved this, and quite possibly put in like 50 other quotes I like. But that is all you will be getting from me. Stop reading my review and go read this book!!!<br><br>And I thank you<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392435ra/755439.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more reviews visit: <a href="http://dirtygirlromance.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dirty Girl Romance Book Blog </a><br><br>P.S.<br><br>I need the next book like yesterday! For the love of Jebus, WHAT?!<br><br>Ok...I think my manic episode is done now. Really. Don't judge me!<br><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16167184419072861032"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>This was really good and I really enjoyed it. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426164723i/13983085.jpg' width='400' height='398.4' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Austin was totally my brand of super HI-larious funny.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426164723i/13983086._SY540_.jpg' width='360' height='511.5' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The story line took some turns I wasn't expecting and I really enjoyed the plot and the characters. There are <i>so</i> many other awesome Bunny Slipper reviews out there, so I'm not going to try and re-invent the wheel here. <br/><br/>But I will say this: <br/><br/>My only gripe with this book is that there was a LOT of build up to some VERY awesome sex scenes.<br/><br/>Sex scenes that never really came to fruition. <br/> <br/>Now, I</span>
  <span id="freeText16167184419072861032" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br><br>This was really good and I really enjoyed it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426164723i/13983085.jpg" width="400" height="398.4" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Austin was totally my brand of super HI-larious funny.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426164723i/13983086._SY540_.jpg" width="360" height="511.5" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story line took some turns I wasn't expecting and I really enjoyed the plot and the characters. There are <i>so</i> many other awesome Bunny Slipper reviews out there, so I'm not going to try and re-invent the wheel here. <br><br>But I will say this: <br><br>My only gripe with this book is that there was a LOT of build up to some VERY awesome sex scenes.<br><br>Sex scenes that never really came to fruition. <br> <br>Now, I'm not saying that I <i>always</i> need some cinnamon in my latte...but when you hand me the Starbucks cup and wave the cinnamon shaker in my face - I expect you to deliver. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426164723i/13983087.jpg" width="420" height="294" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424270769i/13736823.jpg" width="420" height="294" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But there was no delivery to be had here. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426164723i/13983088._SX540_.jpg" width="480" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh well. <br><br>Looking forward to reading book two!<br><br>Thanks for the rec Allison!<br><br>XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX<br><br>Recommended by my home skillet Allison! <br><br>Here I go!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426092703ra/13973050.gif" width="245" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <a title="Ami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/134600-ami"><img alt="Ami" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485783876p2/134600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274098428?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ami" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ami" href="/user/show/134600-ami">Ami</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=mm-romance-or-erotica">mm-romance-or-erotica</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274098428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2341074185952594114">This is one of those "strange" things that can happen when you're in a company of a good book. Here are few reasons that <u>should</u> make me dislike this book:<br/><br/><b>One</b>, it is looong. It clocks around 450+ pages on my Kindle. Man, I don't think I even read a lot of mainstream novels that are more than 450 pages. <br/><br/><b>Two</b>, the main characters are actually not that likeable. Austin Glass, the detective, is (I'm using Dani Alexander's words in the book to describe him) "<i>cruel, superficial, spoiled, and really fuck</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2341074185952594114" style="display:none">This is one of those "strange" things that can happen when you're in a company of a good book. Here are few reasons that <u>should</u> make me dislike this book:<br /><br /><b>One</b>, it is looong. It clocks around 450+ pages on my Kindle. Man, I don't think I even read a lot of mainstream novels that are more than 450 pages. <br /><br /><b>Two</b>, the main characters are actually not that likeable. Austin Glass, the detective, is (I'm using Dani Alexander's words in the book to describe him) "<i>cruel, superficial, spoiled, and really fucked up emotionally</i>". Austin even admits that he cheats often to escape commitment. And Austin is actually engaged with an older woman who used to sleep with his father. Icky alert!<br /><br />While Peter, the love interest, is (again using Dani Alexander's words in the book) "<i>obsessive, snarky, bossy, controlling, sleeps with men for money, uses sex to deflect conversations, and manipulative</i>". Their relationship is volatile at the very least. <br /><br /><b>Three</b>, the story is far fetched -- within two weeks, Austin learns that he is gay, sleeps with a suspect, conceales evidence of his lover's crime, houses a murdered, pisses off his fellow cops, and best friends with criminal. Seriously, the story is just over the top crazy; with twists and turns that rival reality TV.<br /><br />BUT ... I can't stop reading it!! Losing a couple of good hours of my nap time to finish it. All those 450+ pages don't matter because I keep on clicking my Kindle to find out what happens next. Borrowing another Dani Alexander's term introduced in this book, I guess the story is just "adorkable". It's like crack. I mean it. <br /><br />It doesn't really deal with simple stuffs either. There are: suicide history, prostitution, dirty cops, rape cases (off screen), murder, Albanian mother, Russian mafia connection, Russian names, bipolar disorder, and a mangy cat named Begone (that might or might not be a demon in disguise :p). The craziness works, and the language flows really nicely. Dani Alexander doesn't use flowery dramatic language, which truly helps for a story like this. Plus, some of those one liners are awesome; the story is simply enganging with all the hilarity it provides.<br /><br />I guess now I will be one of those people waiting (not-so) patiently for Cai and Riley's story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2341074185952594114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5039486901667076689">Shattered Glass was a great read in the m-m romantic supense category. Was it perfect, no. After just finishing it, I'm dwelling more on the negatives than the positives, which is bothering me. It was a fun book very worthy of 4 stars. The writing is great, the characters felt real (I could picture each one), and the story is gritty enough that it felt true to life.   <span id="freeText5039486901667076689" style="display:none">Shattered Glass was a great read in the m-m romantic supense category. Was it perfect, no. After just finishing it, I'm dwelling more on the negatives than the positives, which is bothering me. It was a fun book very worthy of 4 stars. The writing is great, the characters felt real (I could picture each one), and the story is gritty enough that it felt true to life. It wasn't all sunshine and daisies, which I liked. <br /><br />However, it wasn't a 5 star read for me for a few reasons. I wanted more ROMANCE. There weren't many verbal declarations of... well... anything. I also hated that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Peter liked women more than men! It really put me out of the m-m mode and made me feel like his feelings towards Austin weren't genuine for the entire book. I couldn't shake the feeling that he was faking it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also think the mystery was a bit thrown together in the end. Still, I really enjoyed the book and had a hard time putting it down to do anything else today!</span>

<div id="review_770610764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770610764" />
    <a title="Shurrn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22115857-shurrn"><img alt="Shurrn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410564134p2/22115857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/770610764?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shurrn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shurrn" href="/user/show/22115857-shurrn">Shurrn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=z-lending-library">z-lending-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=i-lol-moments">i-lol-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=genre-humor">genre-humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=series-1st-book">series-1st-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=c-playing-detective">c-playing-detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=genre-crime-or-mystery">genre-crime-or-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22115857-shurrn?shelf=romance-mm">romance-mm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer770610764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12032649722574211156"><b>A book which gleefully oscillates between seriousness and silliness... The only thing more rewarding than reading this book was finally figuring out what all "Bunny Slipper" status updates were about...</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395279375i/8974895.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <blockquote>
  <b><i>“I’m not gay.” That wasn’t what I meant to say. At least not so bluntly. It had just become a mantra as I drove across town. Repeated over and over so many times that, by the time I stood in the diner, confronted once again by this visceral attraction to a perfect stranger, the words tumbled o</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12032649722574211156" style="display:none"><b>A book which gleefully oscillates between seriousness and silliness... The only thing more rewarding than reading this book was finally figuring out what all "Bunny Slipper" status updates were about...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395279375i/8974895.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b><i>“I’m not gay.” That wasn’t what I meant to say. At least not so bluntly. It had just become a mantra as I drove across town. Repeated over and over so many times that, by the time I stood in the diner, confronted once again by this visceral attraction to a perfect stranger, the words tumbled out.<br><br>“Congratulations. Would you like a medal?” Bunny Slippers asked.<br><br>“I already have a medal. For bravery, not for being gay. I think you made me gay.”<br><br>“I </i>made<i> you gay?” He set down the napkin he was holding. “Is that better or worse than the person who made you stupid?”</i></b>
</blockquote> This book was one of the four big players in the MM Romance genre for 2013, and I am grateful to have had the opportunity to do a buddy read of this with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/127120-global-collective-readers" rel="nofollow noopener">GCR Group</a> who were celebrating M/M March. This book would be entertaining for the solo reader, but I also recommend this for a book club. The eroticism doesn't permeate the text, and there is enough character development and seriousness to prompt many interesting conversations...<br><br><b>Shattered Glass is a combination of:</b><br><i>crime drama,<br>coming out angst,<br>haunted pasts,<br>touching connections,<br>laugh out loud humor,<br>murder mystery,<br>brotherly love,<br>general awkwardness,<br>and steamy sexual situations...</i><br><br><b>AUSTIN GLASS</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395279820i/8974942._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I was not insecure. I was a perfectly normal combination of arrogant and narcissistic.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> Logan is a straight-laced detective on track to join the FBI. He's also a trust-fund kid with a huge ego and a fiancé. So when he finds himself sexually attracted to a redheaded bus boy at a local diner, he is obviously knocked for a loop.... And the knocks just keep coming for Detective Glass...<br><br><b>PETER "RABBIT" COTTON</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395279820i/8974943.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Everyone is your competition.” Peter lifted his hand to his eyes and began lowering it incrementally. “It goes normal human beings, crazies, republicans, my hand, imaginary characters, corpses and then, in a moment of lustful psychosis, you.” By the time he was done, his hand was below the table.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> Peter comes from a rough past - one which slowly reveals its dark depths as the book progresses. He isn't a mere busboy at the diner, he's the owner - the ex-cop who took him in off the streets left it to him in his will.<br><br>Together Peter and Austin spell trouble - their attraction is more than merely dangerous for Austin's career, it could quite possibly be deadly...<br><br>There were so many heavy subjects packed into this book... lovingly wrapped in humor... I think a less competent author might have crumbled under the pressure of the undertaking. As it is, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5451387.Dani_Alexander" title="Dani Alexander" rel="nofollow noopener">Dani Alexander</a> has creating an amazingly balanced novel which I can't help but recommend...<br><br>There was a single POV from Austin's perspective though out the book, and his awkwardness shined through brilliantly.<br><br>The show was kind of stolen in the personality department by Peter's little brother Cai - whose past and present are heart-wrenching. He is emotionally unstable and wise beyond his years. <blockquote>
  <b>

We all hope it will be published, but I couldn't tell you when to save my life - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5451387.Dani_Alexander" title="Dani Alexander" rel="nofollow noopener">Dani Alexander</a>'s Slashfiction site says "published 2012" GoodReads says "Published 2014" but they are all lying liars who tell all the lies... <br><br>I will await the next installment.   <span id="freeText9461143084814644110" style="display:none">4.5 stars. Rounded up just because I feel guilty doing four stars just because I was bummed there wasn't more smut scenes in the book. I'm such an MM whore. </a><br><br>I REALLY flipping enjoyed this one. The author must have a great sense of humor to create a character such as Austin. His flippant remarks were off the hook funny. By the end of the book, I felt like I knew him....wanted to know him personally. Austin is a vice squad cop in Denver when he sets eyes on Peter (aka Bunny Slippers) while in a diner waiting for an informant to show. He's drawn to these slippers, to this man with perfect reddish hair and freckles. He doesn't know what's wrong with him. He's not gay. He's engaged for goodness sakes. But he can't stop watching him and thinking about him when he's gone. <br><br><b>“I'm not gay.” That wasn't what I meant to say.<br>“Congratulations. Would you like a medal?” Bunny Slippers asked.<br>“I already have a medal. For bravery, not for being gay. I think you made me gay.”<br>“I made you gay?” He set down the napkin he was holding. “Is that better or worse than the person who made you stupid?”</b><br><br>Did I mention Austin was hilarious! Oh yeah, I did. This book is a nice combination of, yes again, humor, suspense, a bit of mystery, romance, and a little bit of hot M/M smut (but not a lot). <br><br>Austin can't deny his feelings for Peter. He's gay... He admits it. He just didn't realize the world of Peter was going to come crashing through his doors....quite literally. He's willing to give up his fiancée, his job, career hope for FBI, heterosexual status...anything for Peter. But with him comes a mess of problems. <br><br><b>“I've given up my living room, guest room, job, career, heterosexuality and my stance on no pets in the house, but I'm not giving up my room. I'm drawing a line.”</b><br><br>My Austin-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/user/allipalk/media/Male%20Eye%20Candy/2b71610c4f306a14e9203c5529ee330b_zpsc89c1488.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400084i/774936.jpg" alt=" photo 2b71610c4f306a14e9203c5529ee330b_zpsc89c1488.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>My Peter-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/user/allipalk/media/Male%20Eye%20Candy/26fc273418099c87762f30fc95131a49_zps67f386cd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400084i/774937.jpg" alt=" photo 26fc273418099c87762f30fc95131a49_zps67f386cd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>er-<br>With Peter comes a cast of fantastic characters. His flaming friend Darryl who's hilariously gay-feminine, his "brother" Cai who's battled horrible things in life, bipolar disorder and is the sweetest thing ever! Lets not forget Cai's mangy cat Begone-<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/user/allipalk/media/Used%20in%20review/45a10b5e3d2e6827050b5cf695f24c35_zps4c31da48.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400084i/774938.jpg" alt=" photo 45a10b5e3d2e6827050b5cf695f24c35_zps4c31da48.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>"for one thing, the...cat?- looked maimed, or burned. The thing was a walking biohazard of stale tuna seeped in sun- soured milk" </b><br><br>Flamboyant Darryl--<br><a href="http://s1320.photobucket.com/user/allipalk/media/Used%20in%20review/9fa437ba22d5f7a3fdc2dff0f74a1173_zps48ec56a4.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400084i/774939.jpg" alt=" photo 9fa437ba22d5f7a3fdc2dff0f74a1173_zps48ec56a4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>So, I'll let you go forth and read this. I don't want to spoil the story..... I just can't say enough how I loved each of the characters in the book. The author did a stellar job at character development. Each person had their own quirks, banter but they're all fiercely loyal. Austin's ability to finally own up to the years of denial related to his being gay and the banter between he and his cop partner Luis was also hilarious.<br><br><b>"Just seeing my partner cheered me up immediately. As he lifted his eyes over the computer monitor, I placed a giant butt plug on his desk. It reminded me of a mini beige traffic cone. " It's an early hump day gift!" <br> "Jesus, save me from the idiots, " Luis said.</b><br><br> Even his ex Angelina was awesomely supportive....<br><br>Speaking to Angelina about his relationship with Peter-<br><b>"luckily he makes up for it with a mouth that could suck a ping pong ball through a Twizzler." Her upper lip drew up to reveal her teeth. "Too soon?" Her laughter shook my body as she hid her face in my shoulder. "I love you Austin." "Me too, Angel. Me too."</b><br><br>Looking so forward to Cai's story with FBI officer Riley Capone. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="9461143084814644110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_576857660" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/576857660" />
    <a title="* Meli Mel *" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10905711-meli-mel"><img alt="* Meli Mel *" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577750127p2/10905711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/576857660?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="* Meli Mel *" class="user" itemprop="url" name="* Meli Mel *" href="/user/show/10905711-meli-mel">* Meli Mel *</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=lol-funny">lol-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=man-on-man-lovin">man-on-man-lovin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10905711-meli-mel?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer576857660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1178158708960921938"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380414139i/816192._SX540_.jpg' width='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>***5 Hilarious Bunny Slipper Stars***</b><br/><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415683i/820646.png' width='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I'm not gay.” That wasn't what I meant to say.<br/>“Congratulations. Would you like a medal?” Bunny Slippers asked.<br/>“I already have a medal. For bravery, not for being gay. I think you made me gay.”<br/>“I made you gay?” He set down the napkin he was holding. “Is that better or worse than the person who made you stupid?”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>Austin Glass is engaged and already preparing for his upcoming wedding. He comes from a wealthy family and is working with the FBI. Everyth</span>
  <span id="freeText1178158708960921938" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380414139i/816192._SX540_.jpg" width="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>***5 Hilarious Bunny Slipper Stars***</b><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415683i/820646.png" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I'm not gay.” That wasn't what I meant to say.<br>“Congratulations. Would you like a medal?” Bunny Slippers asked.<br>“I already have a medal. For bravery, not for being gay. I think you made me gay.”<br>“I made you gay?” He set down the napkin he was holding. “Is that better or worse than the person who made you stupid?”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Austin Glass is engaged and already preparing for his upcoming wedding. He comes from a wealthy family and is working with the FBI. Everything soon changes when he meets "Bunny Slippers" --who works in a diner-- which was what he was staring at when he was waiting for an informant to arrive. There is something about him that called him and it all started with those bunny slippers. He finds him beautiful and intriguing. Soon, he finds himself questioning if he might in fact be gay and finds the truth in all of the emotions and memories of his past that he has kept deeply buried inside himself.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote> And f*ck it, I'm not gay. Goddammit.<br><i>I'm bunny-slipper-sexual?<br><br>*****************<br><br>“The fact that I was more comfortable owning up to the slippers thing and not the c*cksucker thing was mildly disturbing. I’d rather have a footwear fetish than a sudden attraction to penises? Yeah, that sounded about right."<br><br>*****************<br><br>...Bunny Slippers propped his shoulder against the wall, cocking his head slightly as he looked toward my car. My breath halted. I was sure he couldn't see me through the darkened windows, but somehow, it felt like he was seeing right into my slipper-obsessed soul.<br>The bunny slippers, a different pair --and how many did he have for f*ck's sake?</i>
</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I freaking <b>LOVED</b> Austin!!! He was so freaking hilarious! I loved his witty humor, even if it was a tad bit on the rude side, who cares, I <b>LOVED</b> it! Then when he accepts he is gay, he wasn't annoying about how he really wasn't. He embraced it and didn't care what others thought of him, even if it still did hurt a bit. He was really honest, brutally at times, and made no apologies for being himself. He felt unworthy of love due to his parents never really giving him any. So I really enjoyed seeing how Peter affected him and making him question love. He went through a very tough situation as a teen. He lost a friend and never really dealt with it. So, he hides behind his sarcasm and jokes so no one can see him completely. But soon Peter changes everything and he finds himself willing to do almost anything for him, even if they have only have met in such a short amount of time.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415683i/820647.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I <b>LOVED</b> Peter aka "Bunny Slippers" too! He was only twenty years old but he was so mature for his age. He had to raise and support himself and Cai--who is bipolar-- with the help of Darryl by any means possible, which led him to prostitution. Peter loves them both dearly, so he would do absolutely anything to make sure they are safe and taken cared of. Which is what he does when Cai is accused of murder. His upbringing was really terrible, I felt for him and all that he had to witness at such a young age. When Austin shows interest in him, he thinks that all he wants is his body, that he can never be interested in the person. It was really sad that he had to learn how to hide his emotions so well so that no one would worry about him. He was the one always caring for others and never asking for anything in return. I really loved him!<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Rabbit's the rock we cling to when we're drowning. He needs a mountain to hold him up, not another storm that'll wear away at him.”<br><br>****************<br><br>"You're a manipulative as*hole, you know that?"<br>"You love it."<br>"Only when your manipulations are to get into my pants."<br>"Yes, my so clever manipulations to get into your pants. What were those again?"<br>"Breathing. Talking. Existing."<br><br>*****************</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><blockquote>
  <b><i>"You're rich, spoiled and used to getting your way," he said stubbornly.<br>"Not true. If I had my way you would have kissed me and ridden me like a cowboy while screaming 'yeehaw'."<br>"What makes you think </i>you<i> won't ride</i> me<i>?"</i></b>
  <br>
  <br>
  <b>
    <i>*****************<br>”Tell me something good about your life”<br>“You”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415683i/820648._SY540_.jpg" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, it was really well written and I loved all of Austin's inner dialogue. It was so funny to see the banter between Austin and Luis as well. The chemistry between the two main characters was very enjoyable. Their relationship was built slowly. There was steam although not a lot but still it was good. The secondary characters were highly entertaining. I really liked Darryl, he had funny moments and was loyal. I absolutely loved Cai, he was really intelligent, talented and had an innocence that just endeared you. I wanted to hug him and keep him in my pocket! It was so cute how he ended up having a crush on Riley. I am <b>SO</b> excited and <b>HIGHLY</b> anticipating Cai's story! I <b>LOVED</b> this book and I can't say enough how good it was to me. I definitely recommend you give this a try.<br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1178158708960921938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_293102257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293102257" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293102257?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Laura by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5171122-christina">Christina</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293102257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12582466392101529547"><b>He could shatter my soul right now, it was so fragile sitting there in his palm.”</b><br/><br/>This review has been rattling around the ‘ole noggin for weeks now, but I cannot get my feelings down and out on the page. Draft after draft thrown out. <br/><br/>So, this is me free-balling it—so to speak. :D<br/><br/>Mystery, romance, wit, humor, freckles, and bunny slippers! I have such a huge crush on this book! Love, love, love every single thing about it! Haha…Let me give it another go without using the word love 50 times! (Yeah </span>
  <span id="freeText12582466392101529547" style="display:none"><b>He could shatter my soul right now, it was so fragile sitting there in his palm.”</b><br /><br />This review has been rattling around the ‘ole noggin for weeks now, but I cannot get my feelings down and out on the page. Draft after draft thrown out. <br /><br />So, this is me free-balling it—so to speak. :D<br /><br />Mystery, romance, wit, humor, freckles, and bunny slippers! I have such a huge crush on this book! Love, love, love every single thing about it! Haha…Let me give it another go without using the word love 50 times! (Yeah right) <br /><br />Shattered Glass by Dani Alexander is a fast moving, complex, hilarious mystery touched with sadness and filled from top to bottom with characters to adore. Austin, Peter, Darryl, Cai, Luis, and so many more captured my imagination, smile, and heart. I fell in love with Austin from the jump. What’s not to like about a rich, cocky, smartass? :)<br /><br />Detective Austin Glass appears to have his life, career, and love all planned out. That is until he sets eyes on Peter. Everything from the case to his love life turns upside down from there. How long can you hide and deny your true self and identity? Austin’s world blows up with such speed and hilarity it will leave you in awe and giggles. Over and over again whether he puts his foot in his mouth or someone comes walking in at just the right time, Austin truly thrives on a priceless gift of embracing the moment and pieces of his shattered life. A crime and case brings Peter into Austin’s life, but will the case now tear them apart? <br /><br />The back and forth battle for trust, information, leverage, and love between Austin and Peter made me dizzy! At times I was in complete awe of Austin—the way he could just throw caution to the wind and put his feelings out there after hiding for so long. But other times, I was a complete mess, stomach in knots, hands in fists—just waiting for Peter to crush his heart. My heart went from awe to anger in a blink of an eye. Yelling at my kindle over and over—“I can’t believe he said that!” or “Just kiss him!” haha…I loved it!<br /><br />But it was the writing that had me swooning! This book pulled me right in and kept me there. I can’t tell you how many times I almost missed my train stop. :D The back and forth barbs and comebacks snap, snap, *SNAP* readers around from one word to the next. Dani Alexander’s world, words, and wit required and captured my full attention. Once I fell into these pages, it took a physical force to yank me out. The “snap-crackle-and-pop” between the characters, action, words, and scenes grabbed a hold of my reading heart and never let go! The energy pushed the story along at such a maddening pace and mix of relief, pain, fear, love, and lust--it was dazzling! A one of a kind read. <br /><br />I want to give you a taste here, but it is nearly impossible and a bit unfair to pull a conversation or quote out of the flow, magic and energy of the story…but I’m going to give it a go. But really it feels like cutting off a limb somehow. Every time I went to pull a couple of lines it would turn into a few and then the whole scene. The words and energy just flow. To take one piece out, somehow felt wrong to me. But hell—I do love to contradict myself. :) <br /><br />This is just one of my favorite scenes:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[“Let me buy you coffee? Or loafers? Or goddamned sunscreen.<br /><br />I thought you couldn’t—<br /><br />Yeah, I’m not supposed to pay for hookers or go home with guys. There’s a lot I keep doing around you that I’m not supposed to.<br /><br />Am I going to finish a sentence on this date?<br /><br />Depends on how often your lips are in range of mine. Where that came from, I didn’t know. Didn’t care either, because Peter <i>smiled</i>. He rolled his eyes, but he did smile.” <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />So that’s it. Please excuse my tenses, spelling, punctuation, and babbling. I do hope my enthusiasm and love of the book came through though.<br /><br />Shattered Glass is an original, one of a kind reading experience. One I plan to visit again and again.<br /><br />Now GO..go read it! :D<br /><br /><br />Christina—You did it again! Another book I would not have found without ya! Thank you. :)<br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7136507604652582202">This was very different than I expected. It took me a minute to readjust my expectations, and then I really liked it.<br/><br/>First, the hero, Austin, was a seemingly heterosexual cop who was engaged to a woman. And, it wasn't one of those tropes where the woman was horrible and we were oh so glad that he realizes he's gay and dumps that bitch. No, she was nice, and sweet, and deserved better. I really like that the author did that and never made us hate her. It's so much easier to use that shortcut that</span>
  <span id="freeText7136507604652582202" style="display:none">This was very different than I expected. It took me a minute to readjust my expectations, and then I really liked it.<br><br>First, the hero, Austin, was a seemingly heterosexual cop who was engaged to a woman. And, it wasn't one of those tropes where the woman was horrible and we were oh so glad that he realizes he's gay and dumps that bitch. No, she was nice, and sweet, and deserved better. I really like that the author did that and never made us hate her. It's so much easier to use that shortcut that other author's do and make her a villain. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570949691i/28286364._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>See? Perfect girls DO exist. Take that, internet!<br><br>Next, the love-interest. He was hard to figure out. He was definitely not sweet and kind, like the fiance was. He's very layered. Like an onion. Or a cake. It took a while to decide if he was an onion or a cake.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570949691i/28286366._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And I wasn't sure what we would find once we got inside....<br><br>There is so much going on in this story. There are murders, and tons of other crimes. Layers and layers of crime. It was hard to figure out where it was all going. <br><br>Unless..... all those layers.... I think I see what the hidden meaning of this book was after all:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570949691i/28286365._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes! Everything makes sense now. <br>Thank you, book!<br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14131049712066896042">This book was fantastic. The blurb had me hooked with the mangy cat and bunny slippers. I knew that I needed the story behind them and it didn't disappoint. I loved how complex this story was. It kept me on my toes through the whole book. I laughed a lot and I was taken completely by surprise a couple of times. I'm becoming a huge fan of cop romances. I love the action and suspense.<br/><br/>And I loved Austin. He was awesome! Loved his smartass remarks! He would drive me up a wall in real life but he was</span>
  <span id="freeText14131049712066896042" style="display:none">This book was fantastic. The blurb had me hooked with the mangy cat and bunny slippers. I knew that I needed the story behind them and it didn't disappoint. I loved how complex this story was. It kept me on my toes through the whole book. I laughed a lot and I was taken completely by surprise a couple of times. I'm becoming a huge fan of cop romances. I love the action and suspense.<br /><br />And I loved Austin. He was awesome! Loved his smartass remarks! He would drive me up a wall in real life but he was a great MC. Peter, on the other hand, took me a while to warm up to. I didn't connect with him right away but as his story was revealed, I began to like him more and more and by the end, I loved him just as much as Austin. The supporting characters were an eclectic bunch but rounded out the story nicely. Cai found his way into my heart and I can't wait to read his story. I just hope that Austin and Peter show up too!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5064374577159510802"><b>Pure entertainment and hilarious like no other</b>. This was me in so many levels I can’t start to explain it so I’ll just say that I had a blast reading this book, I fell in love with it and its extraordinary characters and <b>I can’t recommend it strongly enough</b>. This’s why I read, this is the reason I lose myself in books. <br/> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522140939i/25279848._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The adjective to describe Shattered Glass is: hilarious. <b>My kind of humor but with the more than welcome touch of dark-seriousness that gives the plot the perfect amount of enter</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5064374577159510802" style="display:none"><b>Pure entertainment and hilarious like no other</b>. This was me in so many levels I can’t start to explain it so I’ll just say that I had a blast reading this book, I fell in love with it and its extraordinary characters and <b>I can’t recommend it strongly enough</b>. This’s why I read, this is the reason I lose myself in books. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522140939i/25279848._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The adjective to describe Shattered Glass is: hilarious. <b>My kind of humor but with the more than welcome touch of dark-seriousness that gives the plot the perfect amount of entertainment and thrill</b>. <br>This story is a pleasure to read, a <i>laugh out loud</i> experience and, a combination of sexy and feels that hit home in every aspect I needed to. <br>I was captivated by these <b>imperfect, acid, and sarcastic characters. They are everything </b>. A delight.<br>Saying I love Austin Glass is an understatement. Saying I’m not obsessed with Peter Cotton would be a lie. My Peter Rabbit... (you should see my sighing face right now. Dreamy girl writing). <br>I lived for the funny tittles introducing a more than funny little chapters. I breathed for Cai to talk, or smile, or paint or stay there blank-staring. For Darryl to word-punch anyone anytime... and I could keep going for a while... <br>So, long story short (because I won’t do this book justice whatever I say) Shattered Glass has <b>a crime plot developed in a great pace, side characters to die for, film references that made me squee</b> and a humor that can make you smile and laugh so effortlessly it deserves an award. An award for keeping me invested, happy and permanently goose-bumped (if that term exists, that was me while reading this masterpiece of comedy-mystery-love story) <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522140939i/25279849.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>Highly recommended!</b> <br><br><br><a href="https://reviewsforbooklovers.blogspot.com.es/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reviews for Book Lovers</a><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503517262ra/23670232.gif" width="100" height="90" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer719615344" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14485118554819124405"><br/><br/>I believe firmly that our book taste alone is not responsible for our <i>LIKING</i> or <i>NOT LIKING</i> a book. <br/><br/>There are more than one happy coincidence for it.<br/><br/><b>First of all it is our mood.</b><br/> <br/>Sometimes we are angry and disappointed or moody and bad-tempered or sad and despaired or we're in love of endlessly happy or just simply horny-all this conditions demand different kind of literature. <br/><br/><b>There are also another factors like:</b><br/> <br/>*our current life situation<br/><br/>*our current life surroundings<br/><br/>*our current partner<br/><br/>*our las</span>
  <span id="freeText14485118554819124405" style="display:none"><br /><br />I believe firmly that our book taste alone is not responsible for our <i>LIKING</i> or <i>NOT LIKING</i> a book. <br /><br />There are more than one happy coincidence for it.<br /><br /><b>First of all it is our mood.</b><br /> <br />Sometimes we are angry and disappointed or moody and bad-tempered or sad and despaired or we're in love of endlessly happy or just simply horny-all this conditions demand different kind of literature. <br /><br /><b>There are also another factors like:</b><br /> <br />*our current life situation<br /><br />*our current life surroundings<br /><br />*our current partner<br /><br />*our last read book<br /><br />*our last getting laid<br /><br />I don't try to find excuses why <i>I'm so especially fascinated by this book</i>, I only try to justify somebody who is not.<br /><br />According to me...<br />I don't need to say a lot except these simple 4 words:<br /><br /><b>
  <u>I. LOVE. THIS. BOOK.</u>
</b><br /><br />This book was absolutely perfect for me.<br /> <br />This book and me had a perfect timing because all this factors were prepared for me to love it.<br /><br />This book and me are tuned to the same wavelength.<br /> <br />This book was written for me. Sorry for those who have a different opinion on this case, I have to disappoint you- <u>this book is mine.</u><br /><br />I enjoyed every single line in it. <br /><br />I enjoyed every single minute while reading it.<br /><br />I enjoyed the story, with all it's twists and turns.<br /><br />I enjoyed even the suspense part.<br /><br />I enjoyed to be with Austin and Peter.<br /><br />I enjoyed it's humor.<br /><br />I enjoyed the amazing chemistry between the main characters.<br /><br />I enjoyed the Austin POV. Mamma mia!! It was hilarious!!<br /><br />I enjoyed the fucking-tastic dialogues! Oh God! They were so funny!<br /><br />I enjoyed the sex scenes! HOLY FUCKING MELTING PANTY!! THEY WERE HAAAAWT!!<br /><br />I enjoyed THE WRITING! IT.BLEW.ME.AWAY! Alone the chapter's titles deserve 5 stars without any content!<br /><br />This book was just everything I need. Period.<br /><br />The real fun has a name for me now. And it's name is <i>Austin Glass.</i> And <i>Dani Alexander.</i><br /><br />I want more books with the same fun factor. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Please, Dani, please! MORE!!</u>

<div id="review_277677592" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/277677592" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/277677592?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaje Harper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaje Harper" href="/user/show/5309738-kaje-harper">Kaje Harper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309738-kaje-harper?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309738-kaje-harper?shelf=intense">intense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer277677592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5562262114914379581">4.5 stars. Austin is one of the most appealing narrators I have ever met. Sweet, smart and honorable and hiding all that under a thick layer of sarcasm and smart-assery. He is confused by suddenly finding, weeks before his wedding, that his chasing after women has been a veneer hiding his true sexuality. One look at Peter, with his freckles and bunny-slippers and his tough exterior over wounded vulnerability, and it is all over for Austin. And the best part is he doesn't fight it. He doesn't gra</span>
  <span id="freeText5562262114914379581" style="display:none">4.5 stars. Austin is one of the most appealing narrators I have ever met. Sweet, smart and honorable and hiding all that under a thick layer of sarcasm and smart-assery. He is confused by suddenly finding, weeks before his wedding, that his chasing after women has been a veneer hiding his true sexuality. One look at Peter, with his freckles and bunny-slippers and his tough exterior over wounded vulnerability, and it is all over for Austin. And the best part is he doesn't fight it. He doesn't grab for the shreds of his closet or bemoan his fate. He's gay, he's going to be out there and dive full speed into this confusing life change and let the chips fall where they may. And Peter, confusing Peter with his lies and his truths and his complex self-created family, is going to be at the center of that journey of self-realization. The presence of murder, arson, gun-shot wounds, betrayal of friends, three mothers with less-than-maternal attitudes, and a host of other complications can never get deep enough to touch what Austin feels for Peter. Even if he would rather have his dick cut off and eaten with tomato sauce before admitting how far his emotional needs go. Even if he never gets a straight answer from Peter.<br /><br />The plot in this book is over the top enough to take a ladder to the roof and keep on climbing, and it matters not a whit. Occasionally it's a little confusing, which is where it lost that half-star from me. But I inhaled this book as fast as I could, and will read anything else Austin cares to narrate to me. Highly recommended for anyone who loves complex imperfect characters and can tolerate a little bit of plot issues. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5562262114914379581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_274697618" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274697618" />
    <a title="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck"><img alt="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472332781p2/4268461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274697618?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emanuela ~plastic duck~" href="/user/show/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck">Emanuela ~plastic duck~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck?shelf=action-crime-suspense">action-crime-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4268461-emanuela-plastic-duck?shelf=rainbow-gay">rainbow-gay</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274697618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer133033013179984766">I wanted to wait to write this review, then I realized I couldn't. I'm impressed and I've been impressed all the while reading this book.<br/><br/>The narrator, Austin, is frustrating, and you have to dig dig dig to get something deeper about him and you don't really get there. You have to have the patience of a saint to endure his snark and his mania. In his words:<br/><br/><i>"I was not insecure. I was a perfectly normal combination of arrogant and narcissistic."</i><br/><br/>How can you stand reading 122+k-words in his point of </span>
  <span id="freeText133033013179984766" style="display:none">I wanted to wait to write this review, then I realized I couldn't. I'm impressed and I've been impressed all the while reading this book.<br /><br />The narrator, Austin, is frustrating, and you have to dig dig dig to get something deeper about him and you don't really get there. You have to have the patience of a saint to endure his snark and his mania. In his words:<br /><br /><i>"I was not insecure. I was a perfectly normal combination of arrogant and narcissistic."</i><br /><br />How can you stand reading 122+k-words in his point of view? Austin lives in his own world, where he fights/connects with very few people, a trust-fund 26-year-old detective, whose ambition is to work for the FBI. He's good at his job, he's well aware of that. He's a serial cheater, engaged to be married to a brilliant lawyer, Angelica. He has an old friend, with whom he shared the friendship of Jesse, a gay friend who committed suicide, leaving a void and - especially for Austin - an unexplored doubt.<br /><br />The self-revolving world of this arrogant and narcissistic young man is shaken when he meets a gorgeous guy serving tables in a diner wearing bunny slippers. Austin's bunny-slipper fetish immediately infected me. Peter has a cold, distant attitude; he's gorgeous; he was a whore. Austin sees Peter and his life turns upside down, but at the same time clicks into place. What attracted me in Austin, what made me really pay attention to him, was this (desperate?) way of embracing what happens to him to the greatest extent. It's both brave and stupid, and also superficial, and probably spoiled, it defies self-preservation, but if there's one good thing, it's that it's selfless. It exposes him to hurt, but it's also a way to defend himself. It's a way to take control of a situation, going with the flow and accepting all the consequences. It might be something that brings him down, but it's something he chose for himself. <br /><br />The plot revolves around Austin's case and Peter's involvement in it, and in all the ways Austin fucks up his life to get Peter. Peter and Austin's relationship is always unbalanced, because Austin holds a kind of power over Peter, and he's rich, he has information, he can influence the case, but this fact exposes Austin to being exploited by Peter. Peter is not always trustworthy, because his primary goal is to protect his brother Cai, a 16-year-old boy affected by a bipolar disorder and carrying a heavy baggage of experiences. Peter keeps Austin distant, but once in a while he yanks his chain, bringing him conveniently closer. Austin risks his career and his friends to stand by Peter and later by Peter's family. Peter's ambiguity is lifted slowly. He is only 20, but he is far more mature and grown-up than Austin, because the life he had to live was ripe with danger and responsibility, while Austin's problems seem those of a despondent child. While Austin lusts over Peter, trying to do the right thing anyway, we can't help feeling in Peter's reluctance the few tenuous strands of self-determination. Peter is willing to surrender to Austin, but he chooses the terms of that surrender.<br /><br />I'm making a lot of serious thoughts about this story, which is very funny and will make you laugh out loud a few times, because Austin doesn't have a filter between his brain and his mouth. Many many times I checked if what he was saying was in quotes, because I couldn't believe the pits he was able to dig for himself.<br /><br />The plot has a lot of twists and turns. I think there was a great balance between the moments of pure action and the moments which made the personal, emotional story move forward. I also think the author gave to his protagonists a lot of layers, hidden motives, deep secrets, painful self-denials, everything contributed to make them perfectly imperfect, but exquisitely real. Secondary characters included, especially Austin's partner Luis, stoic and heroic for putting up with Austin's antics; and Darryl, flamboyant and deadly. <br /><br />Everything is linked and woven into a net (emphasis not mine):<br /><br /><i>"Maybe Peter was the answer. The problem <b>and</b> the answer. The answer without being the solution."</i><br /><br />I liked this level of complication. It's exactly what I'm looking for in the main couple.<br /><br />I've raved enough. Highly recommended. Looking forward to reading Cai's story, and what the younger guy is up to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="133033013179984766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BasQOIVqKUwsfRjDHHSdykRilqmbG/Uhno7Sb9G6yNYMtP9HITFTLQf1ySG1yp8wF0XEWgF1OYWRLDiL8zPf0Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
